<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_architecture">Civil architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Civil architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Venezia_Nuova"><i>Venezia Nuova</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Venezia Nuova">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panorama_Venezia_Nuova,_Livorno.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2412" data-file-width="5052" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Panorama_Venezia_Nuova%2C_Livorno.JPG/300px-Panorama_Venezia_Nuova%2C_Livorno.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Panorama_Venezia_Nuova%2C_Livorno.JPG/450px-Panorama_Venezia_Nuova%2C_Livorno.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Panorama_Venezia_Nuova%2C_Livorno.JPG/600px-Panorama_Venezia_Nuova%2C_Livorno.JPG 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Panorama_Venezia_Nuova,_Livorno.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Venezia Nuova</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ferdinando_II_de%27_Medici,_Grand_Duke_of_Tuscany" title="Ferdinando II de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany">Ferdinando II de' Medici</a> considered, in 1629, the opportunity to enlarge the town, on project by Giovanni Battista Santi, toward north in an area included among <i><a href="/wiki/Livorno#Fortezza_Vecchia" title="Livorno">Fortezza Vecchia</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Livorno#Fortezza_Nuova" title="Livorno">Fortezza Nuova</a></i>, in order to give an adequate space to the maritime and commercial activities. There was the need to build a mercantile district, close to <i><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Livorno#Porto_Mediceo" title="Port of Livorno">Porto Mediceo</a></i>, provided with houses and depots to store the merchandise and a system of canals to facilitate their transport. The new <i><a href="/wiki/Rione" title="Rione">rione</a></i> (district), called <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Venezia_Nuova&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Venezia Nuova (page does not exist)">Venezia Nuova</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venezia_Nuova" title="it:Venezia Nuova">it</a>)</span></i>, was built in an area gained to the sea, intersected by canals and linked to the town with bridges, for this reason Venetians skilled workers were recruited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="extiw" href="https://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chiesa_di_Sant%27Anna_(Venezia)" title="it:Chiesa di Sant'Anna (Venezia)">Chiesa di Sant'Anna</a>, dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Saint_Anne" title="Saint Anne">Saint Anne</a>, was built in 1631 on the ground of the Arch confraternity of the Company of the Nativity;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> in the same year Giovanni Battista Santi died and the control of the project passed to Giovanni Francesco Cantagallina though the works slowed down due to the lack of funds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>A new impulse to the works was given in 1656 concerning the distribution of the spaces where to build other houses and stores; consequently arose the problem of the diverse oriented road scheme respect to the axis of <i>Piazza d’Arme</i>, it was resolved adopting a road plan perpendicular to the <a href="/wiki/Navicelli_channel" title="Navicelli channel">Navicelli channel</a>. The paving of the roads and along the canals in <i>Venezia Nuova</i> was provided in 1668,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> while the <i>Pescheria Nuova</i> (New fish-market) was built in 1705 close to the <i>Scali del Pesce</i> where the fish was unloaded.</p>
<p>In the 1700s <i>Venezia Nuova</i> was the district of the Consuls of the Nations and of the most important international retailers who had the warehouses filled with goods from everywhere waiting to be shipped by sea to the most different destinations. The palaces along the canals had the turrets from which to see the ships approaching the port, moreover they had the stores at the canal level to facilitate the unloading of the goods from the boats.</p>
<p>The <i>Venezia Nuova</i> district retains much of its original town planning and architectural features such as the bridges, narrow <a href="/wiki/Lane" title="Lane">lanes</a>, the houses of the <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">nobility</a>, churches as <a href="/wiki/Santa_Caterina_da_Siena,_Livorno" title="Santa Caterina da Siena, Livorno">Santa Caterina da Siena</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Ferdinando,_Livorno" title="San Ferdinando, Livorno">San Ferdinando</a>, and a dense network of canals that once served to link its warehouses to the port.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Monumento_dei_quattro_mori"><i>Monumento dei quattro mori</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Monumento dei quattro mori">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Quattro_mori_monument_02.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3888" data-file-width="2592" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Livorno_Quattro_mori_monument_02.JPG/220px-Livorno_Quattro_mori_monument_02.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Livorno_Quattro_mori_monument_02.JPG/330px-Livorno_Quattro_mori_monument_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Livorno_Quattro_mori_monument_02.JPG/440px-Livorno_Quattro_mori_monument_02.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Quattro_mori_monument_02.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i>Monumento dei Quattro Mori</i> recently restored</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Monument_of_the_Four_Moors" title="Monument of the Four Moors">Monument of the Four Moors</a> is dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Ferdinando_I_de%27_Medici,_Grand_Duke_of_Tuscany" title="Ferdinando I de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany">Ferdinando I de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany</a>, and is one of the most popular monuments of Livorno. Ferdinando I commissioned it to Giovanni Bandini in 1595 to carry out a monument in white <a href="/wiki/Carrara_marble" title="Carrara marble">Carrara marble</a> to represent him in the uniform of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Master_(order)" title="Grand Master (order)">Grand master</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Saint_Stephen" title="Order of Saint Stephen">Order of Saint Stephen</a> which in that period prevailed in several naval battles against the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">Barbary pirates</a>. The monument was completed in 1599, shortly before the death of Bandini which occurred on April 18,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-comunequattro_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-comunequattro-17">[17]</a></sup> and arrived to Livorno by sea from <a href="/wiki/Carrara" title="Carrara">Carrara</a> in 1601.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toscanago_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-toscanago-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ferdinando I projected to add four statues of moors prisoners at the pedestal of his monument and gave the task to <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Tacca" title="Pietro Tacca">Pietro Tacca</a> in 1602 <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-comunequattro_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-comunequattro-17">[17]</a></sup> but the monument remained in a corner of the square till May 29, 1617 when it was inaugurated by <a href="/wiki/Cosimo_II_de%27_Medici,_Grand_Duke_of_Tuscany" title="Cosimo II de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany">Cosimo II de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toscanago_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-toscanago-18">[18]</a></sup> In the meantime Tacca received the approval to add the four moors to the pedestal; the first two statues were fused in <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a> in 1622 and carried on the barges along the <a href="/wiki/Arno" title="Arno">Arno</a> to Livorno; according to the tradition the young moor was named Morgiano and the older Alì Salentino;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toscanago_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-toscanago-18">[18]</a></sup> the other two sculptures were installed in 1626. During the French occupation of Livorno, from 1796 to 1799, the monument was removed from Sextius Mollis commander of the French garrison because it represented an insult to the <a href="/wiki/Tyrant" title="Tyrant">tyranny</a>, as soon as the French left the town the monument was put back in its proper place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-comunequattro_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-comunequattro-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>During World war II the monument was transferred in a protected place in order to avoid to be damaged by allied attacks, the statue of Ferdinando I was hidden in the <a href="/wiki/Pisa_Charterhouse" title="Pisa Charterhouse">Pisa Charterhouse</a> and the four moors in the <a href="/wiki/Poggio_a_Caiano#The_Medici_villa" title="Poggio a Caiano">Medici Villa at Poggio a Caiano</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The monument has been restored recently in 1990 and 2013.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquedotto_Leopoldino"><i><a href="/wiki/Cisternoni_of_Livorno#Acquedotto_Leopoldino" title="Cisternoni of Livorno">Acquedotto Leopoldino</a></i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Acquedotto Leopoldino">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <i>Acquedotto Leopoldino</i> and the neoclassical cisterns of Livorno were part of a sophisticated scheme to provide water to Livorno.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="La_Gran_Conserva"><i><a href="/wiki/Cisternoni_of_Livorno#La_Gran_Conserva" title="Cisternoni of Livorno">La Gran Conserva</a></i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: La Gran Conserva">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>La Gran Conserva</i>, or <i>Il Cisternone</i>, situated on what were the outskirts of 19th-century Livorno, is the largest and best known of the city's covered cisterns.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cisternino_di_citt.C3.A0"><i><a href="/wiki/Cisternoni_of_Livorno#Cisternino_di_citt.C3.A0" title="Cisternoni of Livorno">Cisternino di città</a></i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Cisternino di città">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>Cisternino di città</i> is an austere neoclassical design which was approved in 1837 and completed in 1848.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Piazza_della_Repubblica"><i>Piazza della Repubblica</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Piazza della Repubblica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Piazza_della_Repubblica_dalla_Fortezza_Nuova_(Livorno).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Piazza_della_Repubblica_dalla_Fortezza_Nuova_%28Livorno%29.JPG/220px-Piazza_della_Repubblica_dalla_Fortezza_Nuova_%28Livorno%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Piazza_della_Repubblica_dalla_Fortezza_Nuova_%28Livorno%29.JPG/330px-Piazza_della_Repubblica_dalla_Fortezza_Nuova_%28Livorno%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Piazza_della_Repubblica_dalla_Fortezza_Nuova_%28Livorno%29.JPG/440px-Piazza_della_Repubblica_dalla_Fortezza_Nuova_%28Livorno%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Piazza_della_Repubblica_dalla_Fortezza_Nuova_(Livorno).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Piazza della Repubblica</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the beginning of the 19th century arose the need to connect the Medicean road system of the <i><a href="/wiki/Livorno#Pentagono_del_Buontalenti" title="Livorno">Pentagono del Buontalenti</a></i> to the new eastern districts of the town, on the other side of the <i>Fosso Reale</i>, and the requirement to dismantle the city gate <i>Porta a Pisa</i>. The solution adopted in 1844 was that of Luigi Bettarini which considered the coverage of the <i>Fosso Reale</i> with an imposing <a href="/wiki/Vault_(architecture)" title="Vault (architecture)">vault</a>, 240 meters long and 90 meters wide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-comunerepubblica_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-comunerepubblica-20">[20]</a></sup> creating an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elliptical" title="Elliptical">elliptical</a> paving. The portion of canal covered by the new structure continued to be navigable.</p>
<p>The new square was commonly called <i>Piazza del <a href="/wiki/Vault_(architecture)" title="Vault (architecture)">Voltone</a></i> until 1850, then <i>Piazza dei <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Tuscany#Habsburg-Lorraine_Grand_Dukes_of_Tuscany.2C_1814.E2.80.931860" title="List of rulers of Tuscany">Granduchi</a></i> in honour of the Lorraine dynasty until 1859, in the period of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_unification" title="Italian unification">Italian unification</a> was named to <i><a href="/wiki/Charles_Albert_of_Sardinia" title="Charles Albert of Sardinia">Carlo Alberto</a></i> until June 1946 when was given the current name <i>Piazza della <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">Repubblica</a></i>. The square, adorned with 52 marble benches, 92 pillars <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> and two statues dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_III,_Grand_Duke_of_Tuscany" title="Ferdinand III, Grand Duke of Tuscany">Ferdinand III</a> by Francesco Pozzi was inaugurated on September 8, 1847<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-comunerepubblica_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-comunerepubblica-20">[20]</a></sup> and that to <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Leopold II, Holy Roman Emperor">Leopold II</a> by Paolo Emilio Demi was installed on June 6, 1848.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-comunerepubblica_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-comunerepubblica-20">[20]</a></sup> The statue of Leopoldo II was damaged by the crowd on May 6, 1849 and removed from the square because the Emperor was seen as the symbol of the Austrian domination; the statue was placed in <i>Piazza <a href="/wiki/Porta_Pia" title="Porta Pia">XX Settembre</a></i> in 1957.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terrazza_Mascagni"><i>Terrazza Mascagni</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Terrazza Mascagni">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Terrazza_Mascagni_01_@chesi.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2377" data-file-width="3816" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Livorno_Terrazza_Mascagni_01_%40chesi.JPG/220px-Livorno_Terrazza_Mascagni_01_%40chesi.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Livorno_Terrazza_Mascagni_01_%40chesi.JPG/330px-Livorno_Terrazza_Mascagni_01_%40chesi.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Livorno_Terrazza_Mascagni_01_%40chesi.JPG/440px-Livorno_Terrazza_Mascagni_01_%40chesi.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Terrazza_Mascagni_01_@chesi.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Terrazza Mascagni</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Terrace_(building)" title="Terrace (building)">Terrazza</a> <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Mascagni" title="Pietro Mascagni">Mascagni</a></i> is a wide sinuous, suggestive belvedere toward the sea from which it is possible to admire the Livorno hills, the <a href="/wiki/Tuscan_Archipelago" title="Tuscan Archipelago">Tuscan Archipelago</a> until the <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Livorno" title="Port of Livorno">Port of Livorno</a>. It take place where once was the <i>Forte dei Cavalleggieri</i> (Cavalrymen Fort) built in the 17th century by <a href="/wiki/Cosimo_I_de%27_Medici,_Grand_Duke_of_Tuscany" title="Cosimo I de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany">Cosimo I de' Medici</a> to control the raids of the pirates,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> then in the 1800s a leisure park named “Eden” and in the early 1900s an heliotherapy centre. A new <a href="/wiki/Parterre" title="Parterre">parterre</a>, built in 1925 and completed in 1928 on project by Enrico Salvais and Luigi Pastore, was formed by a series of flower beds and a walkway which follow the outline of the sea with numerous balustrades named to <a href="/wiki/Costanzo_Ciano" title="Costanzo Ciano">Costanzo Ciano</a>. The <i>Terrazza</i> has a paving surface of 8,700 square meters formed by 34,800 black and white tiles placed as a <a href="/wiki/Checkerboard" title="Checkerboard">checkerboard</a> and 4,100 <a href="/wiki/Baluster" title="Baluster">balusters</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> In the large square were built in 1932 the <a href="/wiki/Gazebo" title="Gazebo">Gazebo</a> for the music, on project by Ghino Venturi,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> which was destroyed during World war II, and in 1937 the <a href="/wiki/Livorno#Acquario_comunale_.22Diacinto_Cestoni.22" title="Livorno">Livorno Aquarium</a>. Immediately the war the <i>Terrazza</i> was dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Mascagni" title="Pietro Mascagni">Mascagni</a> and in 1994 underwent a complete restoration using the same kind of material originally employed; the works were completed on July 10, 1998 with the reconstruction of the “Gazebo for the music”.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Palazzo_Comunale"><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Town_hall" title="Town hall">Palazzo Comunale</a></i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Palazzo Comunale">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Palazzo_Comunale_05_@chesi.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Livorno_Palazzo_Comunale_05_%40chesi.JPG/220px-Livorno_Palazzo_Comunale_05_%40chesi.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Livorno_Palazzo_Comunale_05_%40chesi.JPG/330px-Livorno_Palazzo_Comunale_05_%40chesi.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Livorno_Palazzo_Comunale_05_%40chesi.JPG/440px-Livorno_Palazzo_Comunale_05_%40chesi.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Palazzo_Comunale_05_@chesi.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Palazzo Comunale</i> and the restored square</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Livorno was elevated to the status of <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">city</a> on March 19, 1606 by <a href="/wiki/Ferdinando_I_de%27_Medici,_Grand_Duke_of_Tuscany" title="Ferdinando I de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany">Ferdinando I de' Medici</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/Gonfaloniere" title="Gonfaloniere">Gonfaloniere</a> Bernardetto Borromei and the Community representatives held their meetings in the Church of Saint Mary and Saint Julia. A house where to accommodate the Community, placed in <i>Via del Porticciolo</i>, was purchased on June 13, 1646 for the sum of seven thousand <a href="/wiki/Ducat" title="Ducat">ducats</a>, soon it was clear that the place was inadequate to the task and on January 27, 1720 the Council deliberated the construction of the new town hall on project by Giovanni del Fantasia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The new neo-renaissance palace, positioned between <i>Palazzo della Dogana</i> and <i>Palazzo Granducale</i> on the north side of <i>Piazza d’Arme</i>, was partially destroyed by the 1742 earthquake. Restored in 1745 by Bernardino Ciurini and Antonio Fabbri a double white marble stairway and a small bell tower on the top of the façade were added. In the 1867 the complex was enlarged with the acquisition of three other buildings at the back. With the settlement of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Podest%C3%A0" title="Podestà">Podestà</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fascist" title="Fascist">fascist</a> period was carried out a new enlargement in 1929 by Enrico Salvais and Luigi Pastore transforming the adjacent former fire station in council hall. Damaged by the bombing during World war II it was rebuilt and renovated under the direction of Primavera and was inaugurated in 1949 by the mayor Furio Diaz.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_architecture">Religious architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Religious architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cathedral_of_Saint_Francis_of_Assisi">Cathedral of Saint Francis of Assisi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Cathedral of Saint Francis of Assisi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Piazza_Grande_02_@chesi.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Livorno_Piazza_Grande_02_%40chesi.JPG/220px-Livorno_Piazza_Grande_02_%40chesi.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Livorno_Piazza_Grande_02_%40chesi.JPG/330px-Livorno_Piazza_Grande_02_%40chesi.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Livorno_Piazza_Grande_02_%40chesi.JPG/440px-Livorno_Piazza_Grande_02_%40chesi.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Piazza_Grande_02_@chesi.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Cathedral of Saint Francis of Assisi and <i>Piazza Grande</i> restored</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The cathedral of the town, commonly called <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Duomo_di_Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Duomo di Livorno (page does not exist)">Duomo di Livorno</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duomo_di_Livorno" title="it:Duomo di Livorno">it</a>)</span>, is dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Francis_of_Assisi" title="Francis of Assisi">Francis of Assisi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mary_(mother_of_Jesus)" title="Mary (mother of Jesus)">Mary, mother of Jesus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Julia_of_Corsica" title="Julia of Corsica">Julia of Corsica</a>, and was built in a central position of the <a href="/wiki/Livorno#Pentagono_del_Buontalenti" title="Livorno">Pentagono del Buontalenti</a> on the south side of Piazza Grande once named Piazza d’Arme. The original plan was drawn up by <a href="/wiki/Bernardo_Buontalenti" title="Bernardo Buontalenti">Bernardo Buontalenti</a> when he projected the new town. The construction begun in June 1581 on a reviewed plan by Alessandro Pieroni under the direction by Antonio Cantagallina. The church had a rectangular plant with a single nave, the original wooden ceiling, executed from 1610 to 1614, was carved by Vincenzo Ricordati <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> and gilded with seven inserted paintings. Jacopo Ligozzi, Domenico Cresti and Jacopo Chimenti decorated, from 1610 to 1614, three large paintings representing “Saint Francis with Child and the Virgin”, the “Assumption of Mary” and the “Apotheosis of Saint Julia”, the others four paintings were works by minor artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-livornoyoungdom_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-livornoyoungdom-30">[30]</a></sup> The simply façade had a marble porch with twin Doric columns surmounted by a terrace added in 1605 on project by Alessandro Pieroni.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Duomo_Livorno,_interno.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2266" data-file-width="3009" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Duomo_Livorno%2C_interno.JPG/220px-Duomo_Livorno%2C_interno.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Duomo_Livorno%2C_interno.JPG/330px-Duomo_Livorno%2C_interno.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Duomo_Livorno%2C_interno.JPG/440px-Duomo_Livorno%2C_interno.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Duomo_Livorno,_interno.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cathedral's nave</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The church was consecrated on February 19, 1606 by <a href="/wiki/Monsignor" title="Monsignor">Monsignor</a> Nunzio Antonio Grimani; on request by <a href="/wiki/Ferdinando_II_de%27_Medici,_Grand_Duke_of_Tuscany" title="Ferdinando II de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany">Ferdinando II de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany</a>, in 1629, was elevated to <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_church" title="Collegiate church">collegiate church</a> and the <i>Curato</i> was substituted from a <i>Proposto</i> having the functions of the Vicar of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Pisa" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Pisa">archbishop of Pisa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-livornoyoungdom_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-livornoyoungdom-30">[30]</a></sup> The plant of the church was modified in <a href="/wiki/Christian_cross" title="Christian cross">Christian cross</a> when in 1716 was added the first of two lateral chapels. The left side chapel, dedicated to the <a href="/wiki/Eucharist" title="Eucharist">Eucharist</a>, was built on project by Giovanni del Fantasia with frescoes by Giovanni Maria Terreni and the altar attributed to Giovanni Baratta, The right side chapel, dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception" title="Immaculate Conception">Immaculate Conception</a>, was built in 1727 and was decorated with paintings by Luigi Ademollo. The Collegiata in 1806 was elevated to <a href="/wiki/Cathedral" title="Cathedral">cathedral</a> and in 1817 was added the bell tower 50 meter high on project by Gaspero Pampaloni.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The cathedral was completely destroyed in 1943 from the allied bombardment during World war II; it was then rebuilt respecting the original structure except for the two marble porches added to the <a href="/wiki/Transept" title="Transept">transepts</a> and was consecrated on December 21, 1952 by <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Livorno#Ordinaries" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Livorno">Bishop Giovanni Piccioni</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-livornoyoungdom_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-livornoyoungdom-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 2006, on the occasion of the bicentennial of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Livorno" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Livorno">Roman Catholic Diocese of Livorno</a>, the “Christ Crowned with Thorns”, by <a href="/wiki/Fra_Angelico" title="Fra Angelico">Fra Angelico</a>, was displayed in the Chapel of the Eucharist.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Church_of_the_Madonna">Church of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mary_(mother_of_Jesus)" title="Mary (mother of Jesus)">Madonna</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Church of the Madonna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Chiesa_della_Madonna_01_@chesi.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3888" data-file-width="2592" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Livorno_Chiesa_della_Madonna_01_%40chesi.JPG/220px-Livorno_Chiesa_della_Madonna_01_%40chesi.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Livorno_Chiesa_della_Madonna_01_%40chesi.JPG/330px-Livorno_Chiesa_della_Madonna_01_%40chesi.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Livorno_Chiesa_della_Madonna_01_%40chesi.JPG/440px-Livorno_Chiesa_della_Madonna_01_%40chesi.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Chiesa_della_Madonna_01_@chesi.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Chiesa della Madonna</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Church of the Madonna is placed on the homonymous street which connect directly the city centre with the district <i><a href="/wiki/Livorno#Venezia_Nuova" title="Livorno">Venezia Nuova</a></i> through the <a href="/wiki/John_of_Nepomuk" title="John of Nepomuk">John of Nepomuk</a> bridge. According to the tradition the church was built to host the statute of <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Mount_Carmel" title="Our Lady of Mount Carmel">Our Lady of Mount Carmel</a> subtracted from a Turkish ship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The church was important as it was a place of worship for foreigners communities. <a href="/wiki/Ferdinando_I_de%27_Medici,_Grand_Duke_of_Tuscany" title="Ferdinando I de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany">Ferdinando I de' Medici</a> gave the church to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franciscan" title="Franciscan">Franciscan</a> which had the nearby Oratory of Saints Cosmas and Damian. The construction begun on March 25, 1607 on project by <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Pieroni" title="Alessandro Pieroni">Alessandro Pieroni</a> and was completed in 1611; the church at first was dedicated to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mary_(mother_of_Jesus)" title="Mary (mother of Jesus)">Saint Mary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francis_of_Assisi" title="Francis of Assisi">Saint Francis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saints_Cosmas_and_Damian" title="Saints Cosmas and Damian">Saints Cosmas and Damian</a> but in 1638 was dedicated to the <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception" title="Immaculate Conception">Immaculate Conception</a> following an enlargement of the building.</p>
<p>The church has a rectangular plant with a single nave and <a href="/wiki/Groin_vault" title="Groin vault">groin vault</a>, on each side there are the three altars of the foreigner Nations. The altar of the French Nation was built in 1613 and the painting, by Matteo Rosselli, represents <a href="/wiki/Louis_IX_of_France" title="Louis IX of France">Saint Louis</a>. The altar of the Corsica Nation, which at the time was under the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Republic of Genoa</a>, has a painting representing <a href="/wiki/John_the_Evangelist" title="John the Evangelist">John the Evangelist</a>. The altar of the Portuguese Nation built in the 17th century had a wooden statue of Saint Mary until 1728 when this was positioned near the main altar and replaced by one of <a href="/wiki/Anthony_of_Padua" title="Anthony of Padua">Anthony of Padua</a>. The altar of the Dutch-German Nation is dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Andrew_the_Apostle" title="Andrew the Apostle">Andrew the Apostle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Outside the body of the building, separated by a railing, is a Chapel dedicate to the <i><a href="/wiki/Sanctuary_of_Montenero" title="Sanctuary of Montenero">Madonna di Montenero</a></i> built in 1631.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The simple façade was covered in white marble in 1972</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Church_of_the_Most_Holy_Annunciation">Church of the Most Holy Annunciation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Church of the Most Holy Annunciation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Chiesa_Santissima_Annunziata_04_@chesi.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3888" data-file-width="2592" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Livorno_Chiesa_Santissima_Annunziata_04_%40chesi.JPG/220px-Livorno_Chiesa_Santissima_Annunziata_04_%40chesi.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Livorno_Chiesa_Santissima_Annunziata_04_%40chesi.JPG/330px-Livorno_Chiesa_Santissima_Annunziata_04_%40chesi.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Livorno_Chiesa_Santissima_Annunziata_04_%40chesi.JPG/440px-Livorno_Chiesa_Santissima_Annunziata_04_%40chesi.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Chiesa_Santissima_Annunziata_04_@chesi.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Chiesa della Santissima Annunziata</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Church of the <a href="/wiki/Annunciation" title="Annunciation">Most Holy Annunciation</a> take place in the central street of <i>Via della Madonna</i>, no far from the <a href="/wiki/Livorno#Armenian_community" title="Livorno">Armenian community</a> Church of <a href="/wiki/Gregory_the_Illuminator" title="Gregory the Illuminator">Gregory the Illuminator</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Livorno#Church_of_the_Madonna" title="Livorno">Church of the Madonna</a>. The church is called Unite Greeks too because was the worship place for the <a href="/wiki/Livorno#Greek_community" title="Livorno">Greek community</a> of <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Rite" title="Byzantine Rite">Byzantine Rite</a> once lived in Livorno. At the end of 16th century numerous Greeks came to Tuscany to take service aboard the <a href="/wiki/Galley" title="Galley">galleys</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Saint_Stephen" title="Order of Saint Stephen">Order of Saint Stephen</a>. The church was built in 1601 on project by <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Pieroni" title="Alessandro Pieroni">Alessandro Pieroni</a>, was completed in 1605 and consecrated on March 25, 1606.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">baroque</a> façade was built in 1708 presumably on project by <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Baratta" title="Giovanni Baratta">Giovanni Baratta</a> with a triangular <a href="/wiki/Pediment" title="Pediment">pediment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doric_order" title="Doric order">Doric order</a> and was decorated by the statues of Meekness and Innocence by Andrea Vaccà. The interior has a single nave and the ceiling is adorned by a <a href="/wiki/Coffer" title="Coffer">coffer</a> structure with a central painting representing the Annunciation by Giovanni Domenico Ferretti (1750).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The precious wooden <a href="/wiki/Iconostasis" title="Iconostasis">Iconostasis</a> in Byzantine style date back to 1641 and has three doors painted by Agostino Wanonbrachen in 1751; on the central door is represented the Most Holy Annunciation and <a href="/wiki/Basil_of_Caesarea" title="Basil of Caesarea">Basil of Caesarea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gregory_of_Nazianzus" title="Gregory of Nazianzus">Gregory of Nazianzus</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Chrysostom" title="John Chrysostom">John Chrysostom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Athanasius_of_Alexandria" title="Athanasius of Alexandria">Athanasius of Alexandria</a>; in the right door is painted the <a href="/wiki/Nativity_of_Jesus" title="Nativity of Jesus">Nativity of Jesus</a> and the four Apostles, in the left door is represented the <a href="/wiki/Adoration_of_the_Shepherds" title="Adoration of the Shepherds">Adoration of the Shepherds</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The church was entirely destroyed by the bombings during World war II and the restoration was completed in 1985.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Church_of_Saint_Caterina"><a href="/wiki/Santa_Caterina_da_Siena,_Livorno" title="Santa Caterina da Siena, Livorno">Church of Saint Caterina</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Church of Saint Caterina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Church of Saint Caterina is a baroque church in the centre of Livorno, in <i>Venezia Nuova</i> district.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Church_of_Saint_Ferdinand"><a href="/wiki/San_Ferdinando,_Livorno" title="San Ferdinando, Livorno">Church of Saint Ferdinand</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Church of Saint Ferdinand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>San Ferdinando is a Baroque style, Roman Catholic church located in <i>Venezia Nuova</i> district next to the Piazza del Luogo Pio.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Church_of_Saint_John_the_Baptist"><a href="/wiki/San_Giovanni_Battista,_Livorno" title="San Giovanni Battista, Livorno">Church of Saint John the Baptist</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Church of Saint John the Baptist">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>San Giovanni Battista</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque</a>-<a href="/wiki/Mannerism" title="Mannerism">Mannerist</a> style, Roman Catholic church located at the crossing of <i>Via San Giovanni</i> and <i>Via Carraia</i> in central Livorno.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Church_of_Our_Lady_of_the_Rescue"><a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_del_Soccorso,_Livorno" title="Santa Maria del Soccorso, Livorno">Church of Our Lady of the Rescue</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Church of Our Lady of the Rescue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>Santa Maria del Soccorso</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Neoclassicism" title="Neoclassicism">Neoclassical</a>-style Marian votive church in central Livorno. The tall brick church façade is located scenically at the end of <i>Via Magenta</i>, and has a park surrounding it. In front is a Monument to Fallen Soldiers (<i>caduti</i>) in the first World War.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_English_Cemetery"><a href="/wiki/Old_English_Cemetery,_Livorno" title="Old English Cemetery, Livorno">Old English Cemetery</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Old English Cemetery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Old English Cemetery is the oldest foreign Protestant burial ground in Italy. It was founded around 1645 and contains over 300 Carrara marble graves of notable people from 10 different nationalities. <a href="/wiki/Tobias_Smollett" title="Tobias Smollett">Tobias Smollett</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francis_Horner" title="Francis Horner">Francis Horner</a> were buried here, but also some of the friends of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Gordon_Byron" title="George Gordon Byron">Byron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Percy_Bysshe_Shelley" title="Percy Bysshe Shelley">Shelley</a> and the husband of <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Ann_Seton" title="Elizabeth Ann Seton">Saint Elizabeth Seton</a>. The cemetery was closed in 1839 and a new one, still active, was opened.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sanctuary_of_Montenero"><a href="/wiki/Sanctuary_of_Montenero" title="Sanctuary of Montenero">Sanctuary of Montenero</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sanctuary of Montenero">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Up in the hills the Sanctuary of Montenero, dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Graces" title="Our Lady of Graces">Our Lady of Graces</a>, the patron saint of Tuscany, is a destination for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pilgrims" title="Pilgrims">pilgrims</a>. It is famous for the adjacent gallery, decorated with <a href="/wiki/Ex-voto" title="Ex-voto">ex-voto</a>, chiefly related to events of miraculous rescues of people at sea.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Temple_of_the_Dutch_German_Congregation"><a href="/wiki/Temple_of_the_Dutch_German_Congregation" title="Temple of the Dutch German Congregation">Temple of the Dutch German Congregation</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Temple of the Dutch German Congregation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Temple of the Dutch German Congregation, known more simply as the <b>Dutch German Church</b>, is situated in Livorno, on the stretch of the <i>Fosso Reale</i> canal that runs between <i>Piazza della Repubblica</i> and <i>Piazza Cavour</i>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Synagogue">The Synagogue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: The Synagogue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Synagogue_of_Livorno" title="Synagogue of Livorno">Synagogue of Livorno</a> is the main <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Jewish</a> place of worship in Livorno located in <i>Piazza <a href="/wiki/Elijah_Benamozegh" title="Elijah Benamozegh">Elijah Benamozegh</a></i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_architecture">Military architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Military architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fortezza_Vecchia"><i>Fortezza Vecchia</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Fortezza Vecchia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Fortezza_Vecchia_bastione_della_Ampolletta_01_@chesi.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Livorno_Fortezza_Vecchia_bastione_della_Ampolletta_01_%40chesi.JPG/220px-Livorno_Fortezza_Vecchia_bastione_della_Ampolletta_01_%40chesi.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Livorno_Fortezza_Vecchia_bastione_della_Ampolletta_01_%40chesi.JPG/330px-Livorno_Fortezza_Vecchia_bastione_della_Ampolletta_01_%40chesi.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Livorno_Fortezza_Vecchia_bastione_della_Ampolletta_01_%40chesi.JPG/440px-Livorno_Fortezza_Vecchia_bastione_della_Ampolletta_01_%40chesi.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Fortezza_Vecchia_bastione_della_Ampolletta_01_@chesi.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Fortezza Vecchia</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The origin of <i><a href="/wiki/Old_Fortress,_Livorno" title="Old Fortress, Livorno">Fortezza Vecchia</a></i> takes place not far from what once was <i>Porto Pisano</i> (Pisan Port) where a square tower was built in 1077, on request of <a href="/wiki/Matilda_of_Tuscany" title="Matilda of Tuscany">Matilda of Tuscany</a>, on the remains of a Roman tower; in 1241 the Pisans built a massive cylindrical tower, 30 meters high erroneously called <i><a href="/wiki/Keep" title="Keep">Mastio</a> di Matilde</i> (Matilda keep). <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livornina_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Livornina-39">[39]</a></sup> Pisa realized the strategic importance of the castle of Livorno which owned since 1103 and in 1377 the <a href="/wiki/Doge" title="Doge">Doge</a> <i>Gambacorti</i> of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Pisa" title="Republic of Pisa">Republic of Pisa</a> built a quadrangular Fort called <i>Quadratura dei Pisani</i> (Quartered of the Pisans) on plans attributed to <i>Puccio di Landuccio</i> and <i>Francesco di Giovanni Giordani</i>. In 1392 this fort was connected to a wall in order to defend better the town and the <i><a href="/wiki/Dock_(maritime)" title="Dock (maritime)">Darsena</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Livorno, in 1405, was sold to Genoa which reinforced the defences building three forts under the Quartered, afterwards Livorno was bought from <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a> on August 28, 1421 at the price of 100.000 <a href="/wiki/Tuscan_florin" title="Tuscan florin">Tuscan florin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treccanilivorno_7-6"><a href="#cite_note-treccanilivorno-7">[7]</a></sup> The project to build <i>Fortezza Vecchia</i> was commissioned to <a href="/wiki/Antonio_da_Sangallo_the_Elder" title="Antonio da Sangallo the Elder">Antonio da Sangallo the Elder</a> in 1506, the fortress had to incorporate the existing Pisan and Genovese constructions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Fortezza_Vecchia_bastione_della_Canaviglia_02_@chesi.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Livorno_Fortezza_Vecchia_bastione_della_Canaviglia_02_%40chesi.JPG/220px-Livorno_Fortezza_Vecchia_bastione_della_Canaviglia_02_%40chesi.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Livorno_Fortezza_Vecchia_bastione_della_Canaviglia_02_%40chesi.JPG/330px-Livorno_Fortezza_Vecchia_bastione_della_Canaviglia_02_%40chesi.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Livorno_Fortezza_Vecchia_bastione_della_Canaviglia_02_%40chesi.JPG/440px-Livorno_Fortezza_Vecchia_bastione_della_Canaviglia_02_%40chesi.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Fortezza_Vecchia_bastione_della_Canaviglia_02_@chesi.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Matilda keep and <i>Canaviglia</i> bastion</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The works started in 1518 on order of the <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_VII" title="Pope Clement VII">Cardinal Giulio De’ Medici</a> under the supervision by <i>Nicolao da Pietrasanta</i>. The construction was suspended since the popular revolt sent the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Medici#16th_century" title="House of Medici">Medici in exile</a> and was resumed in 1530 on their return. <i>Fortezza Vecchia</i> is a massive fortification completed on April 1, 1534 under <i><a href="/wiki/Alessandro_de%27_Medici,_Duke_of_Florence" title="Alessandro de' Medici, Duke of Florence">Alessandro de' Medici</a></i>; it was built in red-brick with sloping walls and the interposition of clear stones, has a quadrangular plant with a perimeter of 1500 meters and was equipped with 24 cannons to protect each side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livornina_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-Livornina-39">[39]</a></sup> One of the corners directs inside to join the Quartered of the Pisans and Matilda and Genoa keep; the three others are protected by triangular <a href="/wiki/Bastion" title="Bastion">bastions</a> with rounded tips. The bastion toward north is called <i>Capitana</i> because there moored the main <a href="/wiki/Galley" title="Galley">Galley</a>, to east is <i>Ampolletta</i> since housed the sand-glass used to control the guard duty, to west is the <i>Canaviglia</i> derived from <i>Cavaniglia</i> the name of the commander of the galleys of the Grand Ducky of Tuscany. The land on the side toward the town was excavated in order to have the fortress surrounded by the sea for a better defence. <i><a href="/wiki/Cosimo_I_de%27_Medici,_Grand_Duke_of_Tuscany" title="Cosimo I de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany">Cosimo I de' Medici</a></i> built in 1544 an imposing palace, overlooking the <i><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Livorno#Vecchia_Darsena" title="Port of Livorno">Vecchia Darsena</a></i>, above the Quartered of the Pisans which went destroyed during World war II. The successor <a href="/wiki/Francesco_I_de%27_Medici,_Grand_Duke_of_Tuscany" title="Francesco I de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany">Francesco I de' Medici</a> built a small palace toward the sea, later became <i><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Livorno#Porto_Mediceo" title="Port of Livorno">Porto Mediceo</a></i>, on the top of Canaviglia bastion situated at the entrance of <i>Vecchia Darsena</i>. On the opposite side was built a church dedicated to Saint Francis where on March 19, 1606 <i><a href="/wiki/Ferdinando_I_de%27_Medici,_Grand_Duke_of_Tuscany" title="Ferdinando I de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany">Ferdinando I de' Medici</a></i> elevated Livorno to the status of <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">city</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livornina_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-Livornina-39">[39]</a></sup> <i>Fortezza Vecchia</i> changed its function to the coming of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Tuscany#House_of_Habsburg-Lorraine" title="Grand Duchy of Tuscany">House of Habsburg-Lorraine</a> in 1737, by a defensive structure to a military college for officers of the Army of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Tuscany" title="Grand Duchy of Tuscany">Grand Duchy of Tuscany</a> (1769) and afterwards in garrison (1795).</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fortezza_Nuova"><i>Fortezza Nuova</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Fortezza Nuova">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Livorno-Fortezza_Nuova.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Livorno-Fortezza_Nuova.jpg/220px-Livorno-Fortezza_Nuova.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Livorno-Fortezza_Nuova.jpg/330px-Livorno-Fortezza_Nuova.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Livorno-Fortezza_Nuova.jpg/440px-Livorno-Fortezza_Nuova.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Livorno-Fortezza_Nuova.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Fortezza Nuova</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The origin of <i>Fortezza Nuova</i> (New fortress) take place at the end of the 1500s, by the adjustment of <i>Baluardo <a href="/wiki/Francis_of_Assisi" title="Francis of Assisi">San Francesco</a></i> (Saint Francis rampart) and <i>Baluardo <a href="/wiki/Saint_Barbara" title="Saint Barbara">Santa Barbara</a></i> (Saint Barbara rampant) of the project commissioned by <a href="/wiki/Cosimo_I_de%27_Medici,_Grand_Duke_of_Tuscany" title="Cosimo I de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany">Cosimo I</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bernardo_Buontalenti" title="Bernardo Buontalenti">Bernardo Buontalenti</a> with the intention to develop a new urban plan of the town that led to a pentagonal shape surrounded by canals.</p>
<p>The original project was then modified by <a href="/wiki/Don_Giovanni_de%27_Medici" title="Don Giovanni de' Medici">Don Giovanni de' Medici</a>, Claudio Cogorano and <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Pieroni" title="Alessandro Pieroni">Alessandro Pieroni</a> to allow the construction of <i>Fortezza Nuova</i> in order to strengthen the military apparatus of the town. The works started on January 10, 1590 and ended in 1604, the result is a considerable fortification, in stones and red bricks, with a polygonal plant surrounded by water; the new modification brought to the construction of <i>Forte San Pietro</i> (Saint Peter fort) to defend the <i>Venezia Nuova</i> quarter. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1629 part of the fortress was demolished to permit the building of <i>Venezia Nuova</i> and <i>San Marco</i> quarters wanted by <a href="/wiki/Ferdinando_II_de%27_Medici,_Grand_Duke_of_Tuscany" title="Ferdinando II de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany">Ferdinando II</a>. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> <i>Fortezza Nuova</i> has been used for military purpose until the end of World war II, inside were built barracks and warehouses and a chapel dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception" title="Immaculate Conception">Immaculate Conception</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>The fortress was heavily damaged during World war II with the destruction of the most part of the buildings, the restoration was completed in 1972 and the superior part is used at present as public park and centre for events and displays.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pentagono_del_Buontalenti"><i><a href="/wiki/Pentagon" title="Pentagon">Pentagono</a> del <a href="/wiki/Bernardo_Buontalenti" title="Bernardo Buontalenti">Buontalenti</a></i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Pentagono del Buontalenti">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Citt%C3%A0_pentagonale_-Copia_del_progetto_di_B.Buontalenti-.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="485" data-file-width="575" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Citt%C3%A0_pentagonale_-Copia_del_progetto_di_B.Buontalenti-.png/220px-Citt%C3%A0_pentagonale_-Copia_del_progetto_di_B.Buontalenti-.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Citt%C3%A0_pentagonale_-Copia_del_progetto_di_B.Buontalenti-.png/330px-Citt%C3%A0_pentagonale_-Copia_del_progetto_di_B.Buontalenti-.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Citt%C3%A0_pentagonale_-Copia_del_progetto_di_B.Buontalenti-.png/440px-Citt%C3%A0_pentagonale_-Copia_del_progetto_di_B.Buontalenti-.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Citt%C3%A0_pentagonale_-Copia_del_progetto_di_B.Buontalenti-.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The copy of the project by Buontalenti</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Francesco_I_de%27_Medici,_Grand_Duke_of_Tuscany" title="Francesco I de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany">Francesco I de' Medici</a> gave to <a href="/wiki/Bernardo_Buontalenti" title="Bernardo Buontalenti">Bernardo Buontalenti</a> in 1575 the task to project the <a href="/wiki/Ideal_town" title="Ideal town">ideal town</a> in order to transform Livorno from a fisherman village in a fortified town to accommodate 12,000 inhabitants,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> to include the original settlement and the <i>Fortezza Vecchia</i>, capable to become the trade centre of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Tuscany" title="Grand Duchy of Tuscany">Grand Duchy of Tuscany</a>. The development of the project led to a pentagonal plant as in use in the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> period, each side 600 meters long, with defensive walls, rampant and five bastions at the vertices, surrounded by canals; the fifth bastion coincided with <i><a href="/wiki/Livorno#Fortezza_Vecchia" title="Livorno">Fortezza Vecchia</a></i>. The plan gave no information regarding the function of the new urban area, indicating only a series of building blocks within a road system absolutely orthogonal, <a href="/wiki/Cardo" title="Cardo">cardo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Decumanus_Maximus" title="Decumanus Maximus">Decumanus Maximus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The road axis from north to south (cardo) underline the direction that united the centre of the town with a significant place as the <a href="/wiki/Sanctuary_of_Montenero" title="Sanctuary of Montenero">Sanctuary of Montenero</a>; the axis from west to east (decumanus) linked the <i>Baluardo Santa Giulia</i> to <i>Baluardo Sant’Andrea</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-architetto_livorno_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-architetto_livorno-47">[47]</a></sup> In August 1576 was created the Office of the <i>Fabbrica di Livorno</i> with the task of supervising the construction and Alessandro Puccini was the chief superintendent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>Francesco I de' Medici laid the first stone for the construction of the <i>Baluardo di San Francesco</i> (Saint Francis rampant) of the new town on March 28, 1577; the works went on with several changes compared with the original plan including the construction of the <i><a href="/wiki/Livorno#Fortezza_Nuova" title="Livorno">Fortezza Nuova</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-architetto_livorno_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-architetto_livorno-47">[47]</a></sup> Livorno became a town, encircled by the navigable <i><a href="/wiki/Canal" title="Canal">Fosso</a> Reale</i> (Royal canal), with numerous palaces, warehouse, garrisons and custom-houses. The central street at that time was <i>Via Ferdinanda</i> extended for 750 meters, later called <i>Via Grande</i>, from <i><a href="/wiki/City_gate" title="City gate">Porta</a> Colonnella</i> (Colonella city gate), in the proximity of <i><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Livorno#Vecchia_Darsena" title="Port of Livorno">Vecchia Darsena</a></i>, to <i>Porta Pisana</i> (Pisan city gate). The <i>Baluardo Sant’Andrea</i> was initiated in 1578 while the <i>Baluardo Santa Giulia</i> started in 1582.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1594 it was decided to create a huge square, at halfway of <i>Via Ferdinanda</i>, where to build the church of the new town. The church, that was built in a central position on the south side of <i>Piazza d’Arme</i>, later <i>Piazza Grande</i>, was completed in 1602 under the direction of Antonio Cantagaliina and <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Pieroni" title="Alessandro Pieroni">Alessandro Pieroni</a>. <i>Piazza d’Arme</i> was completed and enlarged with the old <i>Porticciolo dei Genovesi</i> (Port of Genovesi) filled up with earth to make room to the building called <i>Tre Palazzi</i> (Three palaces); the square was adorned with a series of marble arcades attributed to Alessandro Pieroni. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The <i>Palazzo del <a href="/wiki/Picket_(military)" title="Picket (military)">Picchetto</a></i> was built, on plan by <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Foggini" title="Giovanni Battista Foggini">Giovanni Battista Foggini</a> and Giovanni del Fantasia in 1707, at the end of <i>Via Ferdinanda</i> in the proximity of <i>Porta Pisana</i>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Accademia_Navale"><i><a href="/wiki/Italian_Naval_Academy" title="Italian Naval Academy">Accademia Navale</a></i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Accademia Navale">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Italian_Naval_Academy" title="Italian Naval Academy">Italian Naval Academy</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Mixed-sex_education" title="Mixed-sex education">mixed-sex</a> military university in Livorno, which is responsible for the technical training of military officers of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Navy" title="Italian Navy">Italian Navy</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreigner_minorities"><a href="/wiki/Alien_(law)" title="Alien (law)">Foreigner</a> minorities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Foreigner minorities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
