<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Armenian_community"><a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenian</a> community</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Armenian community">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ferdinando_I_de%27_Medici,_Grand_Duke_of_Tuscany" title="Ferdinando I de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany">Ferdinando I de' Medici, Grand Duke of Tuscany</a> issued in 1591 a decree encouraging Armenians to settle in Livorno to increase its trade with the Ottoman Empire and western Asia. By the beginning of the 17th century, Armenians operated 120 shops in town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> In 1701 the Armenian community, who were members of the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Apostolic Church</a>, were authorized to build their own church, which they dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Gregory_the_Illuminator" title="Gregory the Illuminator">Gregory the Illuminator</a>. The project was by <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Foggini" title="Giovanni Battista Foggini">Giovanni Battista Foggini</a> and the church was completed a few years later, but did not open for worship until 1714.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The church had a Latin cross plant and a dome at the intersection of the transept and nave. Destroyed during World War II, it was partly restored in 2008 but is not open to worship.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_community"><a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greek</a> community</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Greek community">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The first Greeks who settled in Livorno early in the 16th century were former mercenaries in the fleet of <a href="/wiki/Cosimo_de%27_Medici" title="Cosimo de' Medici">Cosimo de' Medici</a> and their descendants. This community grew and became significant in the 18th and 19th centuries, when Livorno became one of the principal hubs of the Mediterranean trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Most of the new Greek immigrants came from western Greece, <a href="/wiki/Chios" title="Chios">Chios</a>, <a href="/wiki/Epirus" title="Epirus">Epirus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cappadocian_Greek" title="Cappadocian Greek">Cappadocian Greek</a>.</p>
<p>Based on its status since the late 16th century as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_free_ports" title="List of free ports">free port</a> (<i>port franc</i>) and the warehouses constructed for long-term storage of goods and grains from the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>, until the late 19th century Livorno enjoyed a strong strategic position related to Greek mercantile interests in the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>, and the North Atlantic. The conflicts between Great Britain and France during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> of the early 19th century, with associated port embargoes, piracy, and confiscation of cargoes, played out to the advantage of those Greek merchants willing to accept risk. By the 1820s, Greek entrepreneurs gradually replaced the Protestant British, Dutch, French and other merchants who left the city.</p>
<p>The Greeks concentrated on the grain market, banking and ship-brokering. Cargoes of wheat from the Black Sea were received at Livorno, before being re-shipped to England. Returning ships carried textiles and other industrial goods, which Greek merchants shipped to <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a> and other destinations in the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. Men from the Greek city of <a href="/wiki/Chios" title="Chios">Chios</a> controlled much of the trade. In 1839 Livorno had ten major commercial houses, led primarily by ethnic Greeks and Jewish Italians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>The ethnic Greek community (<i>nazione</i>) had a distinctive cultural and social identity based on their common <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church" title="Greek Orthodox Church">Greek Orthodox religion</a>, language and history. In 1775 they established the Confraternity of Holy Trinity (<i>Confraternita della SS. Trinita</i>) and the <a class="extiw" href="https://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chiesa_greco-ortodossa_della_Santissima_Trinit%C3%A0" title="it:Chiesa greco-ortodossa della Santissima Trinità">Chiesa della Santissima Trinita</a>, the second non-Roman Catholic church in Tuscany. The Armenians had earlier built their own Orthodox church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The community founded a Greek school, awarding scholarships for higher studies to young Greeks from the <a href="/wiki/Peloponnese" title="Peloponnese">Peloponnese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Epirus" title="Epirus">Epirus</a>, Chios or <a href="/wiki/Smyrna" title="Smyrna">Smyrna</a>. The community raised funds to support the Greek Revolution of 1821, as well as various Greek communities in the Ottoman Empire and in Italy.</p>
<p>It also assisted non-Greeks. The Rodocanachi family financed the "School of Mutual Education" established in Livorno by the pedagogist <a class="extiw" href="https://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enrico_Mayer" title="it:Enrico Mayer">Enrico Mayer</a>. The community contributed to founding a school for poor Roman Catholic children. The local governing authorities recognized the contributions of distinguished members of the Greek community (e.g. members of the Papoudoff, Maurogordatos, Rodocanachi, Tossizza and other families) and granted them titles of nobility. After unification and the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a> in 1861, the Greek community in Livorno declined, as the privileges of the free port were rescinded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Jewish_community"><a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Livorno" title="History of the Jews in Livorno">The Jewish community</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: The Jewish community">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>See the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Livorno" title="History of the Jews in Livorno">history of the Jews in Livorno</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects">Dialects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Dialects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Vernacolo"><i>Vernacolo</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Vernacolo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Livorno inhabitants speak a variant of the Italian <a href="/wiki/Tuscan_dialect" title="Tuscan dialect">Tuscan dialect</a>, known as a <i><a href="/wiki/Vernacular" title="Vernacular">vernacolo</a></i>. <i><a href="/wiki/Il_Vernacoliere" title="Il Vernacoliere">Il Vernacoliere</a></i>, a satirical comic-style magazine printed chiefly in the Livornese dialect, was founded in 1982 and is now nationally distributed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Official_website_history_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Official_website_history-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bagitto"><i>Bagitto</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Bagitto">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Judeo-Italian_languages#Dialects" title="Judeo-Italian languages">bagitto</a></i> was a Judæo-Italian regional dialect once used by the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Livorno" title="History of the Jews in Livorno">Jewish community in Livorno</a>. It was a language based on Italian, developed with words coming from Tuscan, Spanish, Portuguese, <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yiddish" title="Yiddish">Yiddish</a>; the presence of Portuguese and Spanish words is due to the origin of the first Jews who came to Livorno, having been expelled from the Iberian peninsula in the late 15th century.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquario_comunale_.22Diacinto_Cestoni.22"><i><a href="/wiki/Aquarium" title="Aquarium">Acquario</a> comunale "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diacinto_Cestoni" title="Diacinto Cestoni">Diacinto Cestoni</a>"</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title='Edit section: Acquario comunale "Diacinto Cestoni"'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Aquarium_Diacinto_Cestoni_01_@chesi.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Livorno_Aquarium_Diacinto_Cestoni_01_%40chesi.JPG/220px-Livorno_Aquarium_Diacinto_Cestoni_01_%40chesi.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Livorno_Aquarium_Diacinto_Cestoni_01_%40chesi.JPG/330px-Livorno_Aquarium_Diacinto_Cestoni_01_%40chesi.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Livorno_Aquarium_Diacinto_Cestoni_01_%40chesi.JPG/440px-Livorno_Aquarium_Diacinto_Cestoni_01_%40chesi.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Aquarium_Diacinto_Cestoni_01_@chesi.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Acquario comunale Diacinto Cestoni</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Livorno Aquarium, dedicated to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diacinto_Cestoni" title="Diacinto Cestoni">Diacinto Cestoni</a>, is the main in Tuscany, situated by <i><a href="/wiki/Livorno#Terrazza_Mascagni" title="Livorno">Terrazza Mascagni</a></i> on the seafront promenade. It was built on project by Enrico Salvais and Luigi Pastore as heliotherapy centre, was opened to the public on June 20, 1937. Destroyed during World war II was rebuilt in 1950;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> in 1999 underwent an extensive reconstruction, on plan by Studio Gregotti and works carried out by Opera Laboratori Fiorentini, was opened definitely on July 31, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> At the ground floor the exhibition include: Diacinto Cestoni Room which consists of 12 exhibition tanks, Mediterranean Area, Indus-Pacific tank, Caribbean Sea, Ligurian coast, Tropical waters, Greek-Roman archaeological coastal area. Livorno Aquarium has 33 exhibition tanks containing 2000 animals of 300 different species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museo_Civico_.22Giovanni_Fattori.22"><i>Museo Civico "<a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Fattori" title="Giovanni Fattori">Giovanni Fattori</a>"</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title='Edit section: Museo Civico "Giovanni Fattori"'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Villa_Mimbelli.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Livorno_Villa_Mimbelli.JPG/220px-Livorno_Villa_Mimbelli.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Livorno_Villa_Mimbelli.JPG/330px-Livorno_Villa_Mimbelli.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Livorno_Villa_Mimbelli.JPG/440px-Livorno_Villa_Mimbelli.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Villa_Mimbelli.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Museo civico Giovanni Fattori</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Museum was inaugurated in 1994 and is placed inside <i>Villa Mimbelli</i>, an 18th-century construction surrounded by a vast park. The origin of the Museum date back to 1877 when the <a href="/wiki/Comune" title="Comune">Comune</a> of Livorno founded a Civic Gallery where to collect all the artistic objects kept in several places around the town; in the same period was written the guideline of the gallery which hosted a collection of paintings of authors by Livorno.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The ground and first floors of the Museum are adorned with decorations, furnishings and draperies of the 18th century style with frescoes by Annibale Gatti.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>In these two floors are shown works by <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Pollastrini" title="Enrico Pollastrini">Enrico Pollastrini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guglielmo_Micheli" title="Guglielmo Micheli">Guglielmo Micheli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ulvi_Liegi" title="Ulvi Liegi">Ulvi Liegi</a>, Oscar Ghiglia, <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Bartolena" title="Giovanni Bartolena">Giovanni Bartolena</a>, Leonetto Campiello and <a href="/wiki/Mario_Puccini" title="Mario Puccini">Mario Puccini</a>. The main exhibition of the Museum is at the second floor where are displayed the paintings by <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Fattori" title="Giovanni Fattori">Giovanni Fattori</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Macchiaioli" title="Macchiaioli">macchiaioli</a> as <a href="/wiki/Silvestro_Lega" title="Silvestro Lega">Silvestro Lega</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telemaco_Signorini" title="Telemaco Signorini">Telemaco Signorini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vincenzo_Cabianca" title="Vincenzo Cabianca">Vincenzo Cabianca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Boldini" title="Giovanni Boldini">Giovanni Boldini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adolfo_Tommasi" title="Adolfo Tommasi">Adolfo Tommasi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angiolo_Tommasi" title="Angiolo Tommasi">Angiolo Tommasi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ludovico_Tommasi" title="Ludovico Tommasi">Ludovico Tommasi</a>. In the other halls are the post-macchiaioli as <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Cecconi" title="Eugenio Cecconi">Eugenio Cecconi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vittorio_Matteo_Corcos" title="Vittorio Matteo Corcos">Vittorio Matteo Corcos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Divisionism" title="Divisionism">divisionism</a> as <a href="/wiki/Benvenuto_Benvenuti" title="Benvenuto Benvenuti">Benvenuto Benvenuti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plinio_Nomellini" title="Plinio Nomellini">Plinio Nomellini</a>. Giovanni Fattori was the main representative artist of the macchiaioli, some of his paintings exhibited are: <i>Carica di Cavalleria a Montebello</i> (1862), <i>La Signora Martelli a Castiglioncello</i> (1867), <i>Assalto alla Madonna della Scoperta</i> (1868), <i>Giornata grigia</i> (1893), <i>Mandrie maremmane</i> (1893), <i>Lungomare ad Antignano</i> (1894), <i>Ritratto della terza moglie</i> (1905).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museo_Ebraico_.22Yeshiv.C3.A0_Marini.22"><i>Museo Ebraico "Yeshivà Marini"</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title='Edit section: Museo Ebraico "Yeshivà Marini"'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Yeshivà Marini Museum is housed in a neoclassical building already place of worship as Marini Oratory since 1867; once was home of the Confraternity Malbish Arumin which provided to help city’s poor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> In the post-war period was utilized as synagogue in the waiting for the construction of the new one. The Museum has a collection of liturgical objects coming from the old Synagogue destroyed in World war II. The commerce practiced by the Jews community increased the property of the synagogue allowing a varied religious heritage of Dutch, Florentine, Venetian, Roman and Northern Africa origin. The display regard the <a href="/wiki/Torah_ark" title="Torah ark">Torah ark</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sefer_Torah" title="Sefer Torah">sefer Torah</a>, paintings, religious objects as the Oriental-style wooden <i>hekhal</i>; the oldest and most important pieces went lost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museo_di_storia_naturale_del_Mediterraneo"><i>Museo di storia naturale del Mediterraneo</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Museo di storia naturale del Mediterraneo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Villa_Webb_Henderson_01.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Livorno_Villa_Webb_Henderson_01.JPG/220px-Livorno_Villa_Webb_Henderson_01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Livorno_Villa_Webb_Henderson_01.JPG/330px-Livorno_Villa_Webb_Henderson_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Livorno_Villa_Webb_Henderson_01.JPG/440px-Livorno_Villa_Webb_Henderson_01.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Villa_Webb_Henderson_01.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Museo di storia naturale del Mediterraneo</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The origins of the museum date back to 1929 and part of the objects went destroyed by World war II. After the war the museum was reopened inside the Livorno Aquarium and only in 1980 was transferred to Villa Henderson. The museum is divided in several halls regarding the Man, the Man in the Mediterranean context, the Invertebrates, the Sea, the Flight in Nature. Inside the museum is a Planetarium and an Auditorium.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museo_Mascagnano"><i>Museo Mascagnano</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Museo Mascagnano">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i>Museo Mascagnano</i> houses memorabilia, documents and operas by the great <a href="/wiki/Composer" title="Composer">composer</a> <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Mascagni" title="Pietro Mascagni">Pietro Mascagni</a>, who lived here. Every year some of his operas are traditionally played during the lyric music season, which is organized by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goldoni" title="Goldoni">Goldoni</a> Theatre. Also the <i><a href="/wiki/Livorno#Terrazza_Mascagni" title="Livorno">Terrazza Mascagni</a></i> is situated on the boulevard on the seafront, is named in his honour.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Orto_Botanico_del_Mediterraneo"><i><a href="/wiki/Orto_Botanico_del_Mediterraneo" title="Orto Botanico del Mediterraneo">Orto Botanico del Mediterraneo</a></i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Orto Botanico del Mediterraneo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i>Orto Botanico del Mediterraneo</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical garden</a> located on the grounds of the <i><a href="/wiki/Livorno#Museo_di_storia_naturale_del_Mediterraneo" title="Livorno">Museo di storia naturale del Mediterraneo</a></i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Port_of_Livorno"><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Livorno" title="Port of Livorno">Port of Livorno</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Port of Livorno">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city and <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Livorno" title="Port of Livorno">port</a> have continued as an important destination for travelers and tourists attracted to its historic buildings and setting. The port processes thousands of <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">cruise-ship</a> passengers of the following <a href="/wiki/Cruise_line" title="Cruise line">cruise line</a>:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/AIDA_Cruises" title="AIDA Cruises">AIDA Cruises</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Azamara_Club_Cruises" title="Azamara Club Cruises">Azamara Club Cruises</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carnival_Cruise_Lines" title="Carnival Cruise Lines">Carnival Cruise Lines</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Celebrity_Cruises" title="Celebrity Cruises">Celebrity Cruises</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Costa_Crociere" title="Costa Crociere">Costa Crociere</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cunard_Line" title="Cunard Line">Cunard Line</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Holland_America_Line" title="Holland America Line">Holland America Line</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Cruise_Line" title="Norwegian Cruise Line">Norwegian Cruise Line</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/P%26O_Cruises" title="P&amp;O Cruises">P&amp;O Cruises</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Princess_Cruises" title="Princess Cruises">Princess Cruises</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pullmantur_Cruises" title="Pullmantur Cruises">Pullmantur Cruises</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Royal_Caribbean_Cruises_Ltd." title="Royal Caribbean Cruises Ltd.">Royal Caribbean Cruises Ltd.</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Silversea_Cruises" title="Silversea Cruises">Silversea Cruises</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thomson_Cruises" title="Thomson Cruises">Thomson Cruises</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Viking_Ocean_Cruises" title="Viking Ocean Cruises">Viking Ocean Cruises</a></li>
</ul>
</div>
<p>many of whom take arranged buses to inland destinations as <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pisa" title="Pisa">Pisa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siena" title="Siena">Siena</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cantiere_navale_fratelli_Orlando"><i>Cantiere navale fratelli Orlando</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Cantiere navale fratelli Orlando">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since 1866 Livorno has been noted for its <a href="/wiki/Cantiere_navale_fratelli_Orlando" title="Cantiere navale fratelli Orlando">Cantiere navale fratelli Orlando</a>. <a href="/wiki/Azimut_Yachts" title="Azimut Yachts">Azimut</a>-<a href="/wiki/Benetti" title="Benetti">Benetti</a> bought the Cantiere navale fratelli Orlando, then of <a href="/wiki/Fincantieri" title="Fincantieri">Fincantieri</a>, in 2003.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eni_petrochemical"><a href="/wiki/Eni" title="Eni">Eni</a> <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical" title="Petrochemical">petrochemical</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Eni petrochemical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The plant produces <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">gasoline</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diesel_fuel" title="Diesel fuel">diesel fuel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fuel_oil" title="Fuel oil">fuel oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lubricant" title="Lubricant">lubricants</a>. Livorno refinery was established in 1936 by <a href="/wiki/Azienda_Nazionale_Idrogenazione_Combustibili" title="Azienda Nazionale Idrogenazione Combustibili">Azienda Nazionale Idrogenazione Combustibili</a> (ANIC) but the plant was completly destroyed during World War II. The plant was rebuilt thanks to an agreement between the ANIC and the <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">Standard Oil</a> forming the STANIC. The production of the new plant raised from 700,000 ton to 2 millions ton in 1955; nowadays the capacity of refining is 84,000 <a href="/wiki/Barrel_(unit)#Oil_barrel" title="Barrel (unit)">barrels</a> per day. The refinery, now property of <a href="/wiki/Eni" title="Eni">Eni</a>, is linked to the <i>Darsena petroli</i> (Oil dock) and to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Firenze" title="Firenze">Firenze</a> depots by two pipelines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Whitehead_Alenia_Sistemi_Subacquei_.28WASS.29"><i>Whitehead Alenia Sistemi Subacquei (WASS)</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Whitehead Alenia Sistemi Subacquei (WASS)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i>Whitehead Alenia Sistemi Subacquei</i> (WASS) plant based in Livorno produce: heavy and light <a href="/wiki/Torpedo" title="Torpedo">torpedoes</a>, anti torpedo countermeasure systems for submarines and ships and sonar systems for underwater surveillance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The factory was founded by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Whitehead" title="Robert Whitehead">Robert Whitehead</a> in 1875 in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fiume" title="Fiume">Fiume</a>, in that period <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, and produced for the first time torpedoes sold all around the world. In 1905 the factory changed name in <i>Torpedo Fabrik Whitehead e Co. Gesellschaft</i> and before his death, Whitehead sold his shares package to <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Limited" title="Vickers Limited">Vickers</a> <a href="/wiki/Armstrong_Whitworth" title="Armstrong Whitworth">Armstrong Whitworth</a>. At the end of World war I the factory was in economic crisis and was purchased by Giuseppe Orlando, one of the owners of the <i><a href="/wiki/Cantiere_navale_fratelli_Orlando" title="Cantiere navale fratelli Orlando">Cantiere navale fratelli Orlando</a></i> of Livorno, as Whitehead Torpedo, in 1924 when was signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome_(1924)" title="Treaty of Rome (1924)">Treaty of Rome</a> and Fiume passed to Italy. Whitehead Torpedo established in Livorno the <i>Società Moto Fides</i> that initially produced motorcycles but changed the production in that of torpedoes. With the end of World war II the Fiume factory was closed and merged with <i>Moto Fides</i> forming the <i>Whitehead Moto Fides Stabilimenti Meccanici Riuniti</i> on July 31, 1945 <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> manufacturing 1000 A244 light torpedo sold to 15 Navies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The <i>Whiteheads Moto Fides</i> continued the production of torpedoes in a new plant opened in 1977 and still operating, then entered in the <a href="/wiki/Fiat_S.p.A." title="Fiat S.p.A.">Fiat Group</a> in 1979 and in 1995 passed definitely to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Finmeccanica" title="Finmeccanica">Finmeccanica</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tuaca"><i><a href="/wiki/Tuaca" title="Tuaca">Tuaca</a></i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Tuaca">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Tuaca" title="Tuaca">Tuaca</a></i> liqueur was produced in Livorno until 2010; the famous distillery was closed and operations were brought to the United States by the new owners. <a href="/wiki/Galliano_(liqueur)" title="Galliano (liqueur)">Galliano</a> is still made here and enjoyed by locals and tourists alike.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Istituto_Tecnico_Industriale_.E2.80.9CGalileo_Galilei.E2.80.9D"><i><a href="/wiki/Secondary_education_in_Italy#Istituto_tecnico" title="Secondary education in Italy">Istituto Tecnico Industriale</a> “<a href="/wiki/Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei">Galileo Galilei</a>”</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Istituto Tecnico Industriale “Galileo Galilei”">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education_in_Italy#Istituto_tecnico" title="Secondary education in Italy">Industrial Technical Institute</a> named to <a href="/wiki/Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei">Galileo Galilei</a> was founded in 1825 as a School of Arts and Crafts in order to prepare the young to a profession in the sector of the mechanic industry as in the decorative arts. In 1923 with the <a href="/wiki/Gentile_Reform" title="Gentile Reform">Gentile Reform</a> was transformed in an Industrial Technical Institute for <a href="/wiki/Mechanics" title="Mechanics">mechanics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a>, and in 1947 was added <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a>. In the following years other specialities were added as <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_physics" title="Nuclear physics">nuclear physics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Informatics" title="Informatics">informatics</a>. The Institute is structured with 32 laboratories, 8 special school-rooms, library, film library, gymnasiums and machine-shops. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Istituto_Nautico_.22Alfredo_Cappellini.22"><i>Istituto Nautico "Alfredo Cappellini"</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title='Edit section: Istituto Nautico "Alfredo Cappellini"'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Nautical Institute Alfredo Cappellini was formed on December 13, 1863 with a Royal Law and it was the first Technical Institute in the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Livorno" title="Province of Livorno">Province of Livorno</a>. In 1921 it was transferred under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of the Navy then returned to the Ministry of Education. The school give the professional preparation to form the <a href="/wiki/Merchant_navy" title="Merchant navy">Merchant navy</a> Officers.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Liceo_Classico_.22Niccolini_Palli.22"><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liceo_Classico" title="Liceo Classico">Liceo Classico</a> "<a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Niccolini" title="Giovanni Battista Niccolini">Niccolini</a> <a href="/wiki/Angeliki_Palli" title="Angeliki Palli">Palli</a>"</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title='Edit section: Liceo Classico "Niccolini Palli"'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <i>Liceo Classico Niccolini</i> was established on March 10, 1860 by law of <a href="/wiki/Terenzio,_Count_Mamiani_della_Rovere" title="Terenzio, Count Mamiani della Rovere">Terenzio Mamiani</a> Ministry of the Public Instruction. The first <i><a href="/wiki/Dean_(education)" title="Dean (education)">Preside</a></i> elected was Luigi De Steffani who remained in charge from 1862 to 1867. The Liceo was entitled to <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Niccolini" title="Giovanni Battista Niccolini">Giovanni Battista Niccolini</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foscolo" title="Foscolo">Foscolo</a>’s friend in 1862 and in 1883 was named to <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Domenico_Guerrazzi" title="Francesco Domenico Guerrazzi">Francesco Domenico Guerrazzi</a>; the double name came into effect in 1889 and remained until the unification of the <i>Liceo</i> with the <i><a href="/wiki/Liceo_delle_scienze_umane" title="Liceo delle scienze umane">Istituto magistrale</a></i>. The most famous professor was <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Pascoli" title="Giovanni Pascoli">Giovanni Pascoli</a> who taught <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> from 1887 to 1895. Among the most prominent pupils were: <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Mascagni" title="Pietro Mascagni">Pietro Mascagni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guglielmo_Marconi" title="Guglielmo Marconi">Guglielmo Marconi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amedeo_Modigliani" title="Amedeo Modigliani">Amedeo Modigliani</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Giosu%C3%A9_Borsi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Giosué Borsi (page does not exist)">Giosué Borsi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Azeglio_Ciampi" title="Carlo Azeglio Ciampi">Carlo Azeglio Ciampi</a> who was teacher in 1945.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Library">Library</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Library">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Biblioteca_Labronica">Biblioteca Labronica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Biblioteca Labronica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Villa_Fabbricotti_01.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Livorno_Villa_Fabbricotti_01.JPG/220px-Livorno_Villa_Fabbricotti_01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Livorno_Villa_Fabbricotti_01.JPG/330px-Livorno_Villa_Fabbricotti_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Livorno_Villa_Fabbricotti_01.JPG/440px-Livorno_Villa_Fabbricotti_01.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Livorno_Villa_Fabbricotti_01.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Biblioteca Labronica F.D. Guerrazzi</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Biblioteca_Labronica&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Biblioteca Labronica (page does not exist)">Biblioteca Labronica</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biblioteca_Labronica" title="it:Biblioteca Labronica">it</a>)</span> was founded in 1816, from the fellows of the <i>Accademia Labronica</i>, which was made public in 1840 and it was given to the Comune in 1852. The civic library was dedicated to Francesco Domenico Guerrazzi in 1923<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> and take place in <i>Villa Fabbricott</i>i, the origin of the villa according to the tradition, date back to the Medicean period when an edifice was built as a suburban residence for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_de%27_Medici" title="Ferdinand II de' Medici">Ferdinand II de' Medici</a>. <i>Villa Fabbricotti</i> received the name from its last owner Bernardo Fabbricotti from <a href="/wiki/Carrara" title="Carrara">Carrara</a> who acquired it from the English merchant Thomas Lloyd in 1881. Fabbricotti, following to adverse economic affairs, sold the Villa and the park to the <a href="/wiki/Comune" title="Comune">Comune</a> in 1936. During World war II the building was used by the German command as headquarter and then taken by the American forces;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> in the post-war period was restored in order to adapt it into library. In the warehouse of the <i>Biblioteca Labronica</i> are stored: 120,000 books, 1,500 <a href="/wiki/Manuscript" title="Manuscript">manuscripts</a>, 117 <a href="/wiki/Incunable" title="Incunable">incunables</a>, 2,000 cinquecentine (is a book printed in the 16th century) and 60,000 <a href="/wiki/Autograph" title="Autograph">autographs</a>; the library is organized with reading rooms with 80 places of capacity, 18 seats for consultation of manuscripts, 4 internet positions and a conference room with 60 seats. The library has a collection of autographs including those of <a href="/wiki/Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei">Galileo Galilei</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Leopardi" title="Giacomo Leopardi">Giacomo Leopardi</a> and manuscript by <a href="/wiki/Ugo_Foscolo" title="Ugo Foscolo">Ugo Foscolo</a> and ancient books printed in Livorno since the 17th century among which the <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A9die" title="Encyclopédie">Encyclopédie</a> printed in 1770 in Livorno by the ancient <i>Bagno dei forzati</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaol" title="Gaol">Gaol</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Convicts" title="Convicts">convicts</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Il_Tirreno"><i><a href="/wiki/Il_Tirreno" title="Il Tirreno">Il Tirreno</a></i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Il Tirreno">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i><b>Il Tirreno</b></i> is a regional <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italian</a> <a href="/wiki/Newspaper" title="Newspaper">newspaper</a>, printed and published in Livorno and distributed in <a href="/wiki/Tuscany" title="Tuscany">Tuscany</a>. <i>Il Tirreno</i> also features sixteen local editions around the whole region.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Il_Vernacoliere"><i><a href="/wiki/Il_Vernacoliere" title="Il Vernacoliere">Il Vernacoliere</a></i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Il Vernacoliere">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i><b>Il Vernacoliere</b></i> is an <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italian</a> satirical monthly magazine printed in Livorno founded in 1982 and distributed in central Italy.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Even if football is the most known and practised sport in the city, many other champions came from others, like athletics (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/400_meters_hurdles" title="400 meters hurdles">400 meters hurdles</a> world champion in 1999 <a href="/wiki/Fabrizio_Mori" title="Fabrizio Mori">Fabrizio Mori</a>) and fencing (<a href="/wiki/Aldo_Montano_(fencer_born_1978)" title="Aldo Montano (fencer born 1978)">Aldo Montano</a>). Livorno also has its own rugby and American football teams.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="A.S._Livorno_Calcio"><i><a href="/wiki/A.S._Livorno_Calcio" title="A.S. Livorno Calcio">A.S. Livorno Calcio</a></i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: A.S. Livorno Calcio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Livorno has a <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> team in <a href="/wiki/Serie_B" title="Serie B">Serie B</a>, <a href="/wiki/A.S._Livorno_Calcio" title="A.S. Livorno Calcio">A.S. Livorno Calcio</a> and the matches are played at the <i><b><a href="/wiki/Stadio_Armando_Picchi" title="Stadio Armando Picchi">Stadio Armando Picchi</a></b></i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Basket">Basket</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: Basket">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pallacanestro_Don_Bosco_Livorno"><i><a href="/wiki/Pallacanestro_Don_Bosco_Livorno" title="Pallacanestro Don Bosco Livorno">Pallacanestro Don Bosco Livorno</a></i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: Pallacanestro Don Bosco Livorno">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>Pallacanestro Don Bosco Livorno</i>, founded in 1996, is an amateur Italian <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> club from the town of Livorno, playing in the <a href="/wiki/Serie_B_Basket" title="Serie B Basket">Serie B</a> (third division) as of June 2015.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport">Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The nearest airport is the main airport of Tuscany, <a href="/wiki/Pisa_International_Airport" title="Pisa International Airport">Pisa International Airport</a>, which is about 20 kilometres (12 mi) away.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buses">Buses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: Buses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Livorno bus service is operated by <i>Compagnia Toscana Trasporti Nord</i> (CTT Nord) that manages 16 urban routes, 2 school routes and 6 suburban routes departing from Livorno; it operates a <a href="/wiki/Funicular" title="Funicular">funicular</a> line which connect low with high <i>Montenero</i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Port">Port</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: Port">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Livorno" title="Port of Livorno">Port of Livorno</a> is one of the largest seaports both in Italy and the Mediterranean Sea as a whole. The Port has regular ferry links of the following operators with the following cities:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Corsica_Ferries_-_Sardinia_Ferries" title="Corsica Ferries - Sardinia Ferries">Corsica Ferries - Sardinia Ferries</a> to <a href="/wiki/Golfo_Aranci" title="Golfo Aranci">Golfo Aranci</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bastia" title="Bastia">Bastia</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grimaldi_Group" title="Grimaldi Group">Grimaldi Lines</a> to <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tangier" title="Tangier">Tangier</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Moby_Lines" title="Moby Lines">Moby Lines</a> to <a href="/wiki/Olbia" title="Olbia">Olbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bastia" title="Bastia">Bastia</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Toremar" title="Toremar">Toremar</a> to <a href="/wiki/Capraia" title="Capraia">Capraia</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trains">Trains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: Trains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city is served by <a href="/wiki/Livorno_Centrale_railway_station" title="Livorno Centrale railway station">Livorno Centrale station</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Livorno&amp;action=edit&amp;section=74" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Italy" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Italy">List of twin towns and sister cities in Italy</a></div>
